<div id="review_1072518203" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1072518203" />
    <a title="ᴥ Irena ᴥ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5252054-irena"><img alt="ᴥ Irena ᴥ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425497470p2/5252054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1072518203?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ᴥ Irena ᴥ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ᴥ Irena ᴥ" href="/user/show/5252054-irena">ᴥ Irena ᴥ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5252054-irena?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5252054-irena?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5252054-irena?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1072518203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8036335226792391709">These might not be the most coherent thoughts I've written.<br/>I am exhausted. I wasn't allowed to choose one side and stick to it. I kept switching. And I loved it.<br/><br/><i>The Scar</i> is more adventure than <i>Perdido Street Station</i> and not just because most of it happens on a floating pirate city. There are mysteries, lies and betrayals, spies, monsters, magic, naval battles and so on. It's not even a spoiler; after you read the description of the book, you expect nothing less.<br/><br/>Bellis Coldwine, one of the protag</span>
  <span id="freeText8036335226792391709" style="display:none">These might not be the most coherent thoughts I've written.<br>I am exhausted. I wasn't allowed to choose one side and stick to it. I kept switching. And I loved it.<br><br><i>The Scar</i> is more adventure than <i>Perdido Street Station</i> and not just because most of it happens on a floating pirate city. There are mysteries, lies and betrayals, spies, monsters, magic, naval battles and so on. It's not even a spoiler; after you read the description of the book, you expect nothing less.<br><br>Bellis Coldwine, one of the protagonists, is first mentioned in the first book as Isaac Dan der Grimnebulin's previous lover, who left him because she got bored of his <i>'rumbustiousness'</i>. Can't say I blame her. They couldn't be more different. I didn't like Bellis at all. When she wasn't angry at people, the world, the situation, she was mopping around Armada. <br>The way she is introduced is completely opposite of garuda Yagharek: when you meet the garuda, you meet the present Yagharek and make your own mind about him before you find out anything about his crime. You get to see a side of him that you'd probably ignore otherwise. I found Bellis irritating right away. She is a really unpleasant person.<br><br>It tells a lot about the writing and the story when a character this unlikeable hasn't managed to ruin anything for me. Further more, her character, such as it is, is a very important part of the plot. If she had been just a bit more passionate, she would have been one of the strongest female characters I've read.<br><br>Bellis Coldwine is an unavoidable linchpin for the main story and someone who pushes the events forward, but she herself isn't very distinguishable.<br><br>The consequences of Isaac's actions in <i>Perdido Street Station</i> can be seen here, albeit indirectly and miles away from New Crobuzon. As someone Isaac knew, Bellis was forced to flee the city. She lied her way on a ship headed for a new colony. The ship also transported a lot of prisoners, most of them Remade. <br>Armada assimilated them most. I can't blame the Remade for wanting to make Armada their home.The Remade are paid for the work they do.<br>Everyone is equal on Armada even though some are a bit more equal than others. <br><b>Armada</b> by Franco Brambilla<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413022083i/11456733._SY540_.jpg" width="250" height="350" alt="Armada" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a href="http://www.superpunch.net/2010/08/dispatches-from-troubled-city-art.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Link to more artwork</a> and one of the reasons why I read this longer.<br><br>There are so many fascinating characters and beings here that a whole review could be written only about them. Miéville can also make us feel sorry for the monsters - anophelii female trying to talk to the man and being shot because they were afraid she was hungry is understandable, terrifying and heartbreaking at the same time. <br><br>Armada consists of different sections with different rulers. The most intriguing character (I bet I am not the only one) in the book does not get any explanation. Uther Doul tells Bellis part of his story, but he still manages to stay mysterious. <br><br>Even after reading the book, my feelings towards Armada are ambiguous. I can't seem to make up my mind. I see the wrongs of it, but I can't forget the Remade and a lot of other things. One thing is certain, the first impression of Armada is <i>definitely not</i> the right one.<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8036335226792391709" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4786359060067927542">This is quite a strange book and it really didn't head in any of the many directions I could have imagined. Mieville's extraordinary world-building is in evidence again, with legions of creatures, aliens, and countries in play.<br/><br/>This one takes place entirely on the ocean, from one ship to a connected flotilla-landmass thing... Okay, clearly I don't have Mieville's way with words. The point is that there is a focus to the things that are under the water, beyond the water, across the water, at the e</span>
  <span id="freeText4786359060067927542" style="display:none">This is quite a strange book and it really didn't head in any of the many directions I could have imagined. Mieville's extraordinary world-building is in evidence again, with legions of creatures, aliens, and countries in play.<br /><br />This one takes place entirely on the ocean, from one ship to a connected flotilla-landmass thing... Okay, clearly I don't have Mieville's way with words. The point is that there is a focus to the things that are under the water, beyond the water, across the water, at the edge of the water, and one of those thingies that goes through the water (canal). There's lots and lots of water in this. So for people with water phobias - steer clear.<br /><br />It was an imaginative book and the story itself was anything but straightforward. Interestingly to me, he used a MC that was actually pretty unlikable. Not that any of the characters were terribly likable...<br /><br />Weird book but really good and totally worth reading.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1006188675" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3839049070163503478">I love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/33918.China_Mi_ville' title='China Miéville' rel='nofollow noopener'>China Miéville</a>. His imagination has no bounds and each book he writes is original. As usual his world building in this book is phenomenal. Who else could have created mosquito people whose men are harmless herbivores while the women (six foot tall but flying just like mosquitoes) crave blood and can suck a human dry in minutes. And then there is the creation called Armada, a floating city formed by attaching hundreds of boats together. I loved his descriptions of how the parks and librari</span>
  <span id="freeText3839049070163503478" style="display:none">I love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/33918.China_Mi_ville" title="China Miéville" rel="nofollow noopener">China Miéville</a>. His imagination has no bounds and each book he writes is original. As usual his world building in this book is phenomenal. Who else could have created mosquito people whose men are harmless herbivores while the women (six foot tall but flying just like mosquitoes) crave blood and can suck a human dry in minutes. And then there is the creation called Armada, a floating city formed by attaching hundreds of boats together. I loved his descriptions of how the parks and libraries, shops and houses were placed in this city and how people progressed around it over rope bridges between decks. I really, really wanted to go visit! An excellent book and well worth reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3839049070163503478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1419251343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16793393271882290277">So far my favorite Miéville's book.<br/><br/>Again main star is one very fascinating city but very different one. New crobuzone is filthy, dream shattering capitalist metropolis, pirate city Armada tries to be opposite. While in Perdido street station he criticizes capitalism in The scar he takes shots at communism and socialism, which I did find bit surprising as Miéville is left wing political activist.<br/> Other than fascinating city this book features multilayered story, well developed characters and crea</span>
  <span id="freeText16793393271882290277" style="display:none">So far my favorite Miéville's book.<br /><br />Again main star is one very fascinating city but very different one. New crobuzone is filthy, dream shattering capitalist metropolis, pirate city Armada tries to be opposite. While in Perdido street station he criticizes capitalism in The scar he takes shots at communism and socialism, which I did find bit surprising as Miéville is left wing political activist.<br /> Other than fascinating city this book features multilayered story, well developed characters and creatures so strange I occasionally had hard time imagining them. All things standard for Miéville's books.</span>

<div id="review_886000438" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/886000438" />
    <a title="Vit Babenco" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19283284-vit-babenco"><img alt="Vit Babenco" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365604577p2/19283284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/886000438?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vit Babenco" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vit Babenco" href="/user/show/19283284-vit-babenco">Vit Babenco</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330392907" href="/book/show/71303.The_Scar">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer886000438" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17859842045177301061">“My armada – three sheets to set sail, bow in the storm – we’ll die in the water. My armada – nothing but murder. To conquer and blunder, led to the slaughter…” <b>Public Image Ltd</b> – <i>Armada</i>.<br/>What is impossible on Earth is possible on the distant worlds…<br/>“A mile below the lowest cloud, rock breaches water and the sea begins. <br/>It has been given many names. Each inlet and bay and stream has been classified as if it were discrete. But it is one thing, where borders are absurd. It fills the spaces between </span>
  <span id="freeText17859842045177301061" style="display:none">“My armada – three sheets to set sail, bow in the storm – we’ll die in the water. My armada – nothing but murder. To conquer and blunder, led to the slaughter…” <b>Public Image Ltd</b> – <i>Armada</i>.<br />What is impossible on Earth is possible on the distant worlds…<br />“A mile below the lowest cloud, rock breaches water and the sea begins. <br />It has been given many names. Each inlet and bay and stream has been classified as if it were discrete. But it is one thing, where borders are absurd. It fills the spaces between stones and sand, curling around coastlines and filling trenches between the continents.”<br /><i>The Scar</i> is a nautical novel done in the tremendous cosmic scale.<br />“The underside of Armada was crisscrossed with life.<br />Fish eddied through its architecture. Fleeting newtlike figures moved with intellect and purpose between boltholes. There were wire mesh cages tucked into hollows and dangling from chains, crowded with fat cod and tunny. Cray dwellings like coral tumors.<br />Beyond the edges of the city, and below it at the far reaches of light, huge half-tame seawyrms corkscrewed and fed. Submersibles droned-rigid shadows. A dolphin made constant vigilant rounds. A moving ecology and politics were tethered to the city’s calcified base.<br />The sea around it resonated with noise made physical: staccato clicks and the vibrations of pounding metal, the swallowed sound of watery friction as currents rubbed against each other. Barks that dissipated when they reached the air.”<br />Huge floating city of pirates sails straight through the great unknown of the Hidden Ocean to its improbable destination. Will Armada achieve its goal?<br /><i>The Scar</i> is a novel created by the imagination that was set free out of the space bedlam.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17859842045177301061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/331808105?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonfaith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonfaith" href="/user/show/2327886-jonfaith">Jonfaith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327886-jonfaith?shelf=speculativelyspeaking">speculativelyspeaking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327886-jonfaith?shelf=darkgrit">darkgrit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331808105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9135902293615435244"><b>This violent, pointless voyage has been sopping with blood. I feel thick and sick with it. And that is all: contingent and brutal without meaning. There is nothing to be learnt here. No ecstatic forgetting. There is no redemption in the sea.</b><br/><br/>Miéville is certainly more focused here than in Perdido Street Station, a streamlined set of characters wrestle with duplicity, inefficient energy policy and the ambiguity of exile. Guile finds a quaint representation, which is always of interest. I loved all</span>
  <span id="freeText9135902293615435244" style="display:none"><b>This violent, pointless voyage has been sopping with blood. I feel thick and sick with it. And that is all: contingent and brutal without meaning. There is nothing to be learnt here. No ecstatic forgetting. There is no redemption in the sea.</b><br /><br />Miéville is certainly more focused here than in Perdido Street Station, a streamlined set of characters wrestle with duplicity, inefficient energy policy and the ambiguity of exile. Guile finds a quaint representation, which is always of interest. I loved all the characters and was impressed with the narrative arc, which didn't attempt to have it both ways. So if Bolaño offered an addendum to a world build, this would be it. We are all the fucking better for it.</span>

<div id="review_1539749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1539749" />
    <a title="Walker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72855-walker"><img alt="Walker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491487436p2/72855.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1539749?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Walker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Walker" href="/user/show/72855-walker">Walker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">roleplayers</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1539749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer35591913321045304">Salubrious. Pugnacious. Ossified. <i>Juddering</i>.<br/><br/>These are not words that I am using to describe China Mieville's writing, but words that China Mieville uses to describe, well, everything. The most irritating part of his otherwise excellent Perdido Street Station is still very much in play in The Scar - that is, Mieville is still kinda unsure of himself, he still feels the need to prove himself, and his method of choice is Big Long Vocabulary Words.<br/><br/>The problem is that he latches onto one, and then us</span>
  <span id="freeText35591913321045304" style="display:none">Salubrious. Pugnacious. Ossified. <i>Juddering</i>.<br /><br />These are not words that I am using to describe China Mieville's writing, but words that China Mieville uses to describe, well, everything. The most irritating part of his otherwise excellent Perdido Street Station is still very much in play in The Scar - that is, Mieville is still kinda unsure of himself, he still feels the need to prove himself, and his method of choice is Big Long Vocabulary Words.<br /><br />The problem is that he latches onto one, and then uses it again and again, sometimes in slightly questionable context. As a result, it can feel like he opened a dictionary at random, found the most obscure word on the page, and then dropped it into his narrative wherever it could possibly fit.<br /><br />Anyway it's not the best-written book I've ever read. It does, however, come close to being one of the most imaginative - even more so than Perdido Street Station, I think. This is why almost all of the critical reviews that get quoted on China Mieville dust jackets praise his creativity, imagination, inventiveness, etc, almost to the exclusion of any mention of how he writes.<br /><br />In his defense, he seems to be getting better as he goes. The Scar is more self-assured than Perdido Street Station, has fewer cringe-moments, is constructed with much greater artistry. And it unfolds the world of Bas-Lag into a much wider, more bizarre arena than we would previously have guessed.<br /><br />All in all, it's a fantastic story in a fantastic setting, supported by medium-strength writing, and I am okay with that.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="35591913321045304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1185431261" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1185431261" />
    <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy"><img alt="Jenny (Reading Envy)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455391853p2/68030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1185431261?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny (Reading Envy)" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy">Jenny (Reading Envy)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=league-extraordinary-dorks">league-extraordinary-dorks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=read2015">read2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1185431261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8603607363943025868">I think this book falls into the category of just not really my thing. There are some books of China Miéville that I have really loved - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9265453.Embassytown' title='Embassytown by China Miéville' rel='nofollow noopener'>Embassytown</a> being my favorite so far. I think there was less going on in that world, and because of that, characters were free to tell more of a story. In this novel, there are so many creatures and places and intrigue to describe, it was hard to settle in to any of it in an enjoyable way. I think I would have really liked the reluctant librarian hostage as unl</span>
  <span id="freeText8603607363943025868" style="display:none">I think this book falls into the category of just not really my thing. There are some books of China Miéville that I have really loved - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9265453.Embassytown" title="Embassytown by China Miéville" rel="nofollow noopener">Embassytown</a> being my favorite so far. I think there was less going on in that world, and because of that, characters were free to tell more of a story. In this novel, there are so many creatures and places and intrigue to describe, it was hard to settle in to any of it in an enjoyable way. I think I would have really liked the reluctant librarian hostage as unlikable as she is, if I had just spent more time with her in the library. I was interested in her understanding (and confusion) with some of the men but many of those storylines fell flat in favor of the action in the story. So some of the time there wasn't enough action, some of the time it was a focus right when I was starting to care about the rest of it. <br /><br />The nice thing about Miéville is that every book is so different, that not exactly enjoying this won't deter me from trying future books. I'm not sure I'd return to Bas-Lag/New Crobuzon, but perhaps another universe.<br /><br />I read this because it was a pick for one of my book clubs, where we meet in a virtual space. I can't wait to see the costumes!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8603607363943025868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7y4KtnjbECxnAtngMHLJbvA/zwbrs5J4gH+T0x/i3qY/WmcXE0JvumM8TtBIkrweNMLOcaEu8KkIybUqjIMTWQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Huj/DNEcZZy/wlP502EqAczYOMPizmuYnk/zKZCtKUnOnJKtuoUaCrv8xMmrgV9xCCU5tKhTCUkW+dXQA8zktg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3203886283723275951">A British "fantastic fiction" writer. He is fond of describing his work as "weird fiction" (after early 20th century pulp and horror writers such as H. P. Lovecraft), and belongs to a loose group of writers sometimes called New Weird who consciously attempt to move fantasy away from commercial, genre clichés of Tolkien epigons. He is also active in left-wing politics as a member of the Socialist W</span>
  <span id="freeText3203886283723275951" style="display:none">A British "fantastic fiction" writer. He is fond of describing his work as "weird fiction" (after early 20th century pulp and horror writers such as H. P. Lovecraft), and belongs to a loose group of writers sometimes called New Weird who consciously attempt to move fantasy away from commercial, genre clichés of Tolkien epigons. He is also active in left-wing politics as a member of the Socialist Workers Party. He has stood for the House of Commons for the Socialist Alliance, and published a book on Marxism and international law.<br /><br /><i>Excerpted from <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China_Mi%C3%A9ville" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia</a>.</i></span>
